Creation, like\\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\\n33: \\t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\\n34: \\t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\\n35: \\t// execution covering just the regular phase.\\n36: \\t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\\n37: \\t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\\n38: \\t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\\n39: \\t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\\n40: \\t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\\n41: \\tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n42: }\\n43: \\n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\\n47: \\t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\\n48: \\t// dispatching configuration.\\n49: \\tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\\n54: // functionality described in the \\\"Assignment to a Queue\\\", \\\"Queuing\\\",\\n55: // and \\\"Dispatching\\\" sections of\\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\\n58: // today is not that day.\\n59: type QueueSet interface {\\n60: \\t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\\n61: \\t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\\n62: \\t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\\n63: \\t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\\n64: \\t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\\n65: \\t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\\n66: \\t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\\n67: \\t// and until it is undesired and empty.\\n68: \\tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n69: \\n70: \\t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\\n71: \\t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\\n72: \\t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\\n73: \\t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\\n74: \\t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\\n75: \\t// from false to true.\\n76: \\tIsIdle() bool\\n77: \\n78: \\t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\\n79: \\t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\\n80: \\t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\\n81: \\t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\\n82: \\t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\\n83: \\t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\\n84: \\t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\\n85: \\t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\\n86: \\t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\\n87: \\t// was idle at the moment of the return.  Otherwise idle==false\\n88: \\t// and the client must call the Finish method of the Request\\n89: \\t// exactly once.\\n90: \\tStartRequest(ctx context.Context, width *request.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn) (req Request, idle bool)\\n91: \\n92: \\t// Dump saves and returns the instant internal state of the queue-set.\\n93: \\t// Note that dumping process will stop the queue-set from proceeding\\n94: \\t// any requests.\\n95: \\t// For debugging only.\\n96: \\tDump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: // QueueNoteFn is called when a request enters and leaves a queue\\n100: type QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\\n101: \\n102: // Request represents the remainder of the handling of one request\\n103: type Request interface {\\n104: \\t// Finish determines whether to execute or reject the request and\\n105: \\t// invokes `execute` if the decision is to execute the request.\\n106: \\t// The returned `idle bool` value indicates whether the QueueSet\\n107: \\t// was idle when the value was calculated, but might no longer be\\n108: \\t// accurate by the time the client examines that value.\\n109: \\tFinish(execute func()) (idle bool)\\n110: }\\n111: \\n112: // QueuingConfig defines the configuration of the queuing aspect of a QueueSet.\\n113: type QueuingConfig struct {\\n114: \\t// Name is used to identify a queue set, allowing for descriptive information about its intended use\\n115: \\tName string\\n116: \\n117: \\t// DesiredNumQueues is the number of queues that the API says\\n118: \\t// should exist now.  This may be non-positive, in which case\\n119: \\t// QueueLengthLimit, and HandSize are ignored.\\n120: \\t// A value of zero means to respect the ConcurrencyLimit of the DispatchingConfig.\\n121: \\t// A negative value means to always dispatch immediately upon arrival\\n122: \\t// (i.e., the requests are \\\"exempt\\\" from limitation).\\n123: \\tDesiredNumQueues int\\n124: \\n125: \\t// QueueLengthLimit is the maximum number of requests that may be waiting in a given queue at a time\\n126: \\tQueueLengthLimit int\\n127: \\n128: \\t// HandSize is a parameter of shuffle sharding.  Upon arrival of a request, a queue is chosen by randomly\\n129: \\t// dealing a \\\"hand\\\" of this many queues and then picking one of minimum length.\\n130: \\tHandSize int\\n131: }\\n132: \\n133: // DispatchingConfig defines the configuration of the dispatching aspect of a QueueSet.\\n134: type DispatchingConfig struct {\\n135: \\t// ConcurrencyLimit is the maximum number of requests of this QueueSet that may be executing at a time\\n136: \\tConcurrencyLimit int\\n137: \\n138: \\t// ConcurrencyDenominator is used in relative metrics of concurrency.\\n139: \\t// It equals ConcurrencyLimit except when that is zero.\\n140: \\tConcurrencyDenominator int\\n141: }\\n142: They\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\n33: \t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\n34: \t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\n35: \t// execution covering just the regular phase.\n36: \t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\n37: \t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\n38: \t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\n39: \t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\n40: \t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\n41: \tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n42: }\n43: \n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\n47: \t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\n48: \t// dispatching configuration.\n49: \tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n50: }\n51: \n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\n54: // functionality described in the \"Assignment to a Queue\", \"Queuing\",\n55: // and \"Dispatching\" sections of\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\n58: // today is not that day.\n59: type QueueSet interface {\n60: \t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\n61: \t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\n62: \t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\n63: \t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\n64: \t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\n65: \t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\n66: \t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\n67: \t// and until it is undesired and empty.\n68: \tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n69: \n70: \t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\n71: \t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\n72: \t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\n73: \t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\n74: \t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\n75: \t// from false to true.\n76: \tIsIdle() bool\n77: \n78: \t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\n79: \t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\n80: \t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\n81: \t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\n82: \t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\n83: \t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\n84: \t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\n85: \t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\n86: \t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\n87: \t// was idle at the moment of the return.  Otherwise idle==false\n88: \t// and the client must call the Finish method of the Request\n89: \t// exactly once.\n90: \tStartRequest(ctx context.Context, width *request.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn) (req Request, idle bool)\n91: \n92: \t// Dump saves and returns the instant internal state of the queue-set.\n93: \t// Note that dumping process will stop the queue-set from proceeding\n94: \t// any requests.\n95: \t// For debugging only.\n96: \tDump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\n97: }\n98: \n99: // QueueNoteFn is called when a request enters and leaves a queue\n100: type QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\n101: \n102: // Request represents the remainder of the handling of one request\n103: type Request interface {\n104: \t// Finish determines whether to execute or reject the request and\n105: \t// invokes `execute` if the decision is to execute the request.\n106: \t// The returned `idle bool` value indicates whether the QueueSet\n107: \t// was idle when the value was calculated, but might no longer be\n108: \t// accurate by the time the client examines that value.\n109: \tFinish(execute func()) (idle bool)\n110: }\n111: \n112: // QueuingConfig defines the configuration of the queuing aspect of a QueueSet.\n113: type QueuingConfig struct {\n114: \t// Name is used to identify a queue set, allowing for descriptive information about its intended use\n115: \tName string\n116: \n117: \t// DesiredNumQueues is the number of queues that the API says\n118: \t// should exist now.  This may be non-positive, in which case\n119: \t// QueueLengthLimit, and HandSize are ignored.\n120: \t// A value of zero means to respect the ConcurrencyLimit of the DispatchingConfig.\n121: \t// A negative value means to always dispatch immediately upon arrival\n122: \t// (i.e., the requests are \"exempt\" from limitation).\n123: \tDesiredNumQueues int\n124: \n125: \t// QueueLengthLimit is the maximum number of requests that may be waiting in a given queue at a time\n126: \tQueueLengthLimit int\n127: \n128: \t// HandSize is a parameter of shuffle sharding.  Upon arrival of a request, a queue is chosen by randomly\n129: \t// dealing a \"hand\" of this many queues and then picking one of minimum length.\n130: \tHandSize int\n131: }\n132: \n133: // DispatchingConfig defines the configuration of the dispatching aspect of a QueueSet.\n134: type DispatchingConfig struct {\n135: \t// ConcurrencyLimit is the maximum number of requests of this QueueSet that may be executing at a time\n136: \tConcurrencyLimit int\n137: \n138: \t// ConcurrencyDenominator is used in relative metrics of concurrency.\n139: \t// It equals ConcurrencyLimit except when that is zero.\n140: \tConcurrencyDenominator int\n141: }\n142: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes--stripped@6d5678ae074d17945f174da2b064603131370a5f/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go"}}}

request\\n47: \\t// characterized by the given digest.  The given `noteFn` will be\\n48: \\t// invoked with the results of request classification.\\n49: \\t// The given `workEstimator` is called, if at all, after noteFn.\\n50: \\t// `workEstimator` will be invoked only when the request\\n51: \\t//  is classified as non 'exempt'.\\n52: \\t// 'workEstimator', when invoked, must return the\\n53: \\t// work parameters for the request.\\n54: \\t// If the request is queued then `queueNoteFn` will be called twice,\\n55: \\t// first with `true` and then with `false`; otherwise\\n56: \\t// `queueNoteFn` will not be called at all. For a configController, the\\n94: // suffix \\\"ReadLocked\\\" stipulates a read lock while just \\\"Locked\\\"\\n95: // stipulates a full lock. that element is in the list.\\n25: // The complexity of the runtime cost is O(1).\\n26: // The returned value is the element removed, if indeed one was removed,\\n27: // otherwise `nil`.\\n28: type removeFromFIFOFunc func() *request\\n29: \\n30: // walkFunc is called for each request in the list in the\\n31: // oldest -> newest order.\\n32: // ok: if walkFunc returns false then the iteration stops immediately.\\n33: // walkFunc may remove the given request from the fifo,\\n34: // but may not mutate the fifo in any othe way.\\n35: type walkFunc func(*request) (ok bool)\\n36: \\n37: // Internal interface to abstract out the implementation details\\n38: // of the underlying list used to maintain the requests.\\n39: //\\n40: // Note that a fifo, including the removeFromFIFOFuncs returned from Enqueue,\\n41: // is not safe for concurrent use by multiple goroutines.\\n42: type fifo interface {\\n43: \\t// Enqueue enqueues the specified request into the list and\\n44: \\t// request from the list.\\n49: \\tDequeue() (*request, bool)\\n50: \\n51: \\t// Peek returns the oldest request without removing it.\\n52: \\tPeek() (*request, bool)\\n53: \\n54: \\t// Length returns the number of requests in the list.\\n55: \\tLength() int\\n56: \\n57: \\t// QueueSum returns the sum of initial seats, final seats, and\\n58: \\t// additional latency aggregated from all requests in this queue.\\n59: \\tQueueSum() queueSum\\n60: \\n61: \\t// Walk iterates through the list in order of oldest -> newest\\n62: \\t// and executes the specified walkFunc for each request in that order.\\n63: \\t//\\n64: \\t// if the specified walkFunc returns false the Walk function\\n65: \\t// stops the walk an returns immediately.\\n66: \\tWalk(walkFunc)\\n67: }\\n68: \\n69: // the FIFO {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01WN5GFkxj3iZGgk8jTo93K6","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01MBLGu89PnYiC4x6FULAjar","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes APF QueueSet Deep-Dive: Algorithmic Behavior, Dispatch Flow, and Fairness Tradeoffs\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem is a sophisticated implementation of Fair Queuing for Server Requests (FQSR) that manages API request concurrency through a virtual-time-based dispatch algorithm. It addresses a fundamental tension in server fairness: how to allocate limited resources fairly among competing clients while maintaining low latency and predictable behavior. This document explains the subsystem's architecture, control flow, fairness algorithm, and operational tradeoffs.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### Purpose\nThe QueueSet subsystem ensures that API server resources are distributed fairly and predictably across different request flows (identified by FlowSchemas and distinguished by client identity or other flow characteristics). Unlike simple first-come-first-served or priority queuing, APF QueueSet provides:\n\n- **Fairness among flows**: Each flow gets a proportional share of server capacity\n- **Burst absorption**: Temporary overloads are queued rather than rejected immediately\n- **Virtual-time fairness**: Queues that have received less service get higher dispatch priority\n- **Work-aware scheduling**: Request \"width\" (concurrency cost) is accounted for, not just count\n\n### Architectural Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n- **APF Filter** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go`): Entry point that classifies requests into FlowSchemas and invokes QueueSet\n- **APF Controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`): Manages FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration CRDs, reconfigures QueueSets dynamically\n- **Work Estimator** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go`): Estimates how many \"seats\" (concurrent slots) a request occupies based on operation type, object count, or watch size\n\n**Downstream users:**\n- HTTP request processing pipeline: Requests flow through StartRequest → queue or immediate dispatch → Finish\n- Metrics collection: QueueSet emits concurrency, latency, and fairness metrics\n\n**No external dependencies:**\n- QueueSet is completely self-contained; it does not interact with other Kubernetes subsystems beyond the filter/controller/estimator layer\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Abstraction Layer (`fairqueuing/interface.go`)\n\n**QueueSetFactory**\n- Creates QueueSets during controller startup and reconfiguration\n- Two-phase construction: `BeginConstruction` (validates config, allocates metrics) → `Complete` (finalizes with concurrency limit)\n- Rationale: Early validation prevents resource exhaustion from bad configs\n\n**QueueSet Interface**\n- Minimal public API: `StartRequest()`, `IsIdle()`, `Dump()`\n- `StartRequest` either: (1) immediately dispatches exempt requests, (2) queues non-exempt requests, or (3) rejects due to concurrency/queue limits\n- Returns a `Request` object that the caller must `Finish()` exactly once\n\n### 2.2 QueueSet Implementation (`queueset/queueset.go`)\n\n**Main QueueSet struct** (lines 85–167)\n- Fields before lock: immutable configuration (clock, metrics gauges, estimated service duration)\n- Fields after lock: mutable state (queues, virtual time R, executing request count, seat tracking)\n\n**Key state fields:**\n- `queues`: Array of `queue` objects, length determined by `DesiredNumQueues` (shuffle-sharding parameter)\n- `currentR`: Global virtual time, expressed in seat-seconds. Monotonically increases, wraps to prevent overflow\n- `totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`: Track resource usage; used for concurrency limit enforcement\n- `totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`: Request counts per phase\n- `robinIndex`: Round-robin pointer for fair queue selection during dispatch\n\n### 2.3 Request Container (`queueset/types.go`)\n\n**request struct** (lines 31–82)\n- Temporary wrapper around a logical request\n- Tracks: context, queue assignment, work estimate, decision promise, arrival time, timestamps\n- Two decision states: `decisionExecute` (dispatch from queue) or `decisionCancel` (timeout)\n- `arrivalR`: Virtual time at enqueue; used to compute virtual finish time\n\n**queue struct** (lines 93–110)\n- `requestsWaiting`: FIFO list of queued requests\n- `requestsExecuting`: Set of actively executing requests from this queue\n- `nextDispatchR`: Virtual finish time of the next request to be dispatched from this queue\n- `seatsInUse`: Current seat count occupied by executing requests\n\n### 2.4 FIFO List with Aggregation (`queueset/fifo_list.go`)\n\n**requestFIFO**\n- Wrapper around Go's `container/list`\n- Maintains running sum (`queueSum`) of initial seats, max seats, and total work across all waiting requests\n- This aggregation enables O(1) queue selection heuristic during shuffle sharding\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Request Initialization Phase\n\n**Entry point: APF Filter (`apf_filter.go:155–198`)**\n```\nHandle(ctx, requestDigest, noteFn, workEstimator, queueNoteFn, execFn)\n```\n\n1. **Classification**: Delegate to controller's `startRequest()` to classify request into FlowSchema/PriorityLevel\n2. **Work estimation**: Call `workEstimator()` to get `WorkEstimate` (InitialSeats, FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency)\n3. **Decision**: Receive `Request` object or nil (rejection)\n4. **Execution**: Call `Request.Finish(execFn)` which:\n   - Waits on virtual queue decision promise\n   - Executes user's HTTP handler\n   - Calls `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()`\n\n### 3.2 Controller Configuration and Startup (`apf_controller.go:371–391`)\n\n**Run() method:**\n1. Waits for FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration informers to sync\n2. Starts config worker goroutine: reads API objects, populates `priorityLevelStates` map\n3. Starts borrowing adjustment goroutine: every 10 seconds, rebalances concurrency limits between priority levels based on seat demand statistics\n\n**lockAndDigestConfigObjects()**: Atomically rebuilds priority level state from FlowSchema specs\n- Ensures backward compatibility: old queue drains before removal\n\n### 3.3 QueueSet.StartRequest() Flow (`queueset.go:308–356`)\n\n**Step 0: Handle exempt priority levels (DesiredNumQueues < 1)**\n- If `DesiredNumQueues ≤ 0`, check only concurrency limit (no queuing)\n- If seats can be accommodated, call `dispatchSansQueueLocked()`: immediately start execution, return request with decision pre-set to `decisionExecute`\n- Otherwise reject and return nil\n\n**Step 1: Shuffle sharding and enqueue (`shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked` lines 552–579)**\n\na. **Shuffle sharding** (`shuffleShardLocked` lines 583–612):\n   - Hash the flow distinguisher (user, namespace, etc.) into a \"hand\" of HandSize queues\n   - Among the hand, pick the queue with minimum total waiting work (seat-seconds)\n   - Rationale: Distributes flows evenly; overloaded flows don't monopolize single queue\n   - Implementation: Uses `shufflesharding.Dealer` (cryptographic shuffle permutation)\n\nb. **Enqueue** (`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked` lines 618–629):\n   - Check: `totSeatsInUse ≥ ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength ≥ QueueLengthLimit`\n   - If true, reject (return nil)\n   - Otherwise, enqueue to FIFO, set request decision promise to `decisionCancel` (default), return request object\n\nc. **Queue initialization**:\n   - If queue was idle, set `nextDispatchR = currentR` (queue inherits global virtual time)\n\n**Step 2: Dispatch loop (`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` lines 654–657)**\n```go\nfor totRequestsWaiting > 0 && totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit && dispatchLocked() {\n}\n```\n- Repeatedly calls `dispatchLocked()` while:\n  - Requests are waiting\n  - Room under concurrency limit\n- Stops when any condition fails or no more requests can be dispatched\n\n### 3.4 Dispatch Algorithm: Virtual Time Fairness (`dispatchLocked` lines 695–743)\n\n**Finding next queue to serve (`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` lines 776–844):**\n\n1. **Round-robin scan** of all queues, searching for highest-priority queue\n2. **Priority metric**: Virtual finish time of oldest request: `minVirtualFinish = nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()`\n3. **Select queue** with minimum virtual finish time\n4. **Round-robin tiebreaker**: If tied, advance robin pointer to favor lower-index queue next iteration\n\n**Dispatching request from chosen queue:**\n\n1. **Seat check**: `canAccommodateSeatsLocked()` verifies max seat requirement fits\n   - Special case: if request width > ConcurrencyLimit and other requests executing, reject\n   - Rationale: Prevent scenarios where single wide request blocks everything\n\n2. **Dequeue and update state**:\n   - Remove from waiting FIFO\n   - Set decision promise to `decisionExecute` (wakes waiting Finish goroutine)\n   - Add to queue's `requestsExecuting` set\n   - Increment `totRequestsExecuting`, `totSeatsInUse`\n\n3. **Update virtual time**:\n   - `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()`\n   - This advances the queue's virtual time, preventing it from repeatedly winning\n\n4. **Anti-windup**: Call `boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)` to prevent virtual time overflow (see section 3.5)\n\n### 3.5 Virtual Time Synchronization and Overflow Prevention (`syncTimeLocked` lines 465–479, `advanceEpoch` lines 492–522)\n\n**syncTimeLocked()** is called whenever lock is acquired:\n```\ncurrentR += virtualTimeRatio * (now - lastRealTime)\n```\n\n- `virtualTimeRatio = min(seatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / numActiveQueues`\n- Rationale: Virtual time advances proportional to server load; more loaded servers have faster virtual clocks\n- Effect: Queues sharing equally will dispatch equally (fairness guarantee)\n\n**Epoch advancement** (line 475):\n- When `currentR ≥ highR` (rDecrement + rDecrement/2), subtract `rDecrement` from:\n  - Global `currentR`\n  - All `queue.nextDispatchR` values\n  - All `request.arrivalR` values\n- Prevents overflow of 64-bit `SeatSeconds` accumulator\n- Records metric: `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total`\n\n### 3.6 Request Completion (`finishRequestLocked` lines 863–902, `wait` method lines 397–441)\n\n**Request.Finish(execFn) sequence:**\n\n1. **Wait for decision** (`wait()` lines 397–441):\n   - Call `req.decision.Get()` (blocking read from promise)\n   - Acquire lock and sync virtual time\n   - If decision is `decisionExecute`, return true\n   - If decision is `decisionCancel` (timeout), remove from queue, return false\n\n2. **Execute handler** (callback):\n   - Run user's HTTP handler with defer for cleanup\n\n3. **Release seats and dispatch more** (`finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible` lines 851–858):\n   - Decrement seat counts\n   - Remove from queue\n   - Call `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` to drain any waiting requests\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Concurrency Limits\n\n**Server-level limit**: Set by operator via `--max-requests` flag\n- Hard cap on total executing requests across all priority levels\n- Prevents server from being overwhelmed\n\n**Priority-level limit**: Configured per PriorityLevelConfiguration\n- `nominalCL`: configured concurrency limit\n- `currentCL`: dynamically adjusted every 10 seconds based on seat demand\n- Borrowing: priority levels can borrow from each other if demand is uneven (see section 4.4)\n\n**Queue-level limit**: `QueueLengthLimit` requests per queue\n- If `totSeatsInUse ≥ ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength ≥ QueueLengthLimit`, reject new request\n- Rationale: Prevents unbounded memory growth; tail latencies become unacceptable\n\n**Seat accounting**: Each request occupies \"seats\" during execution\n- `InitialSeats`: while request is being processed\n- `FinalSeats`: during `AdditionalLatency` (cleanup/response streaming)\n- Rationale: Wide requests (LIST) fairly charged more; prevents resource exhaustion\n\n### 4.2 Request Rejection\n\nRequests are rejected (filter returns 429 Too Many Requests) when:\n\n1. **Concurrency limit reached** AND queue is full: `totSeatsInUse ≥ ConcurrencyLimit AND queueLength ≥ QueueLengthLimit`\n2. **Queue full only** (in some cases): if queue already has QueueLengthLimit requests\n3. **Work exceeds server capacity**: if single request width > ConcurrencyLimit and other requests executing\n\n**Metrics**: `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` labeled by priority level and rejection reason\n\n### 4.3 Request Timeouts\n\n**Queue wait timeout**: Controlled by client context deadline\n- If request context is cancelled or times out while queued, decision is set to `decisionCancel` in `wait()`\n- Request is removed from queue, metrics updated, request fails\n\n**No server-side timeout**: APF does not impose timeouts; relies on client (or gateway) timeout\n\n**Metrics**: `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_queue_depth_after_enqueue` and latency histograms\n\n### 4.4 Seat Demand and Dynamic Borrowing\n\n**Seat demand tracking** (`priorityLevelState.seatDemandIntegrator`):\n- Integrator tracks seat demand (executing + waiting seats) over time\n- Every 10 seconds, `updateBorrowingLocked()` samples and smooths seat demand\n\n**Concurrency limit adjustment**:\n- Non-exempt priority levels: `currentCL = max(minCL, min(nominalCL, smoothedDemand))`\n- Exempt priority levels: uncapped, but `currentCL = max(minCL, highWatermarkDemand)`\n- Rebalancing algorithm: allocates remaining server concurrency among priority levels proportional to smoothed demand\n- If server capacity exhausted, priority levels can share fairly via this algorithm\n\n**Tradeoff**: Borrowing adds latency (10-second reaction time) but prevents static over-allocation\n\n### 4.5 Virtual Time Fairness Guarantees and Limitations\n\n**Fairness property**: If queue i has `ni` waiting requests and queue j has `nj` waiting requests, and both occupy same number of seats, they will be dispatched in proportion `ni : nj` over time (amortized).\n\n**Limitation 1: Work variance**:\n- If requests have widely varying work estimates, variance in service time is unavoidable\n- Example: LIST (wide) and GET (narrow) requests queued together will have different latencies\n\n**Limitation 2: Priority levels (not within-priority fairness)**:\n- QueueSet only guarantees fairness among queues *within* a priority level\n- Inter-priority fairness is handled by concurrency limit allocation (borrowing mechanism)\n- Exempt priority levels bypass QueueSet entirely (no fairness guarantee)\n\n**Limitation 3: Round-robin bias**:\n- `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()` uses round-robin with virtual finish time tiebreaking\n- This introduces slight bias toward lower-index queues; acceptable in practice\n\n### 4.6 Architectural Tradeoffs\n\n| Tradeoff | Choice | Rationale |\n|----------|--------|-----------|\n| **Queuing vs rejection** | Queue first, reject on overflow | Better isolation; allows recovery when load drops |\n| **Shuffle sharding** | Distribute flows across HandSize queues | Prevents single bad actor from blocking entire priority level |\n| **Virtual time scale** | Seat-seconds, not requests | Work-aware fairness; wide requests fairly charged |\n| **Dynamic borrowing** | 10-second rebalancing interval | Coarse grained to avoid thrashing; fast enough for most workloads |\n| **Two-phase config** | BeginConstruction → Complete | Allows rollback if downstream config invalid |\n| **Round-robin dispatch** | Linear scan of all queues | O(n) per dispatch, acceptable for typical queue counts (~8) |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 QueueSetFactory Pluggability\n\n**Location**: `fairqueuing/interface.go:27–42`\n\nOperators can substitute custom `QueueSetFactory` implementations by passing to `TestableConfig`:\n```go\nconfig.QueueSetFactory = customFactory\n```\n\n**Customization examples**:\n- Different shuffle sharding strategies (e.g., deterministic vs random)\n- Alternative FIFO implementations (e.g., priority heap instead of FIFO)\n- Custom virtual time advancement formulas\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect implementation breaks fairness guarantees; requires deep understanding of algorithm\n\n### 5.2 Work Estimator Customization\n\n**Location**: `request/width.go:75–136`\n\n`NewWorkEstimator()` takes pluggable functions:\n- `statsGetterFunc`: Get object count for LIST requests\n- `watchCountGetterFunc`: Get watch listener count for WATCH requests\n- `maxSeatsFunc`: Override maximum seats per priority level\n\n**Current implementation**:\n- LIST/WATCH: seats proportional to object count\n- CREATE/UPDATE/PATCH/DELETE: seats based on watch listeners affected\n- Other verbs: 1 seat\n\n**Risk**: Seat overestimation wastes capacity; underestimation allows resource exhaustion\n\n### 5.3 Clock Abstraction\n\n**Location**: `fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go` (not shown, but imported)\n\nQueueSet uses interface clock, not `time.Now()` directly:\n```go\nclock eventclock.Interface\n```\n\n**Customization**: Inject mock clock for deterministic testing\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect clock causes virtual time disorders; must be monotonic\n\n### 5.4 Priority Level Configuration CRD\n\n**Location**: Kubernetes API, read by controller\n\nOperators can define custom `PriorityLevelConfiguration` and `FlowSchema` objects:\n- Adjust concurrency limits\n- Define flow distinguishers (user, namespace, etc.)\n- Create custom priority levels\n\n**Risk**: Config errors cascade to all requests; controller must validate before applying\n\n### 5.5 MaxSeatsTracker Hook\n\n**Location**: `apf_controller.go:156–160`, `apf_filter.go:81–83`\n\nController tracks maximum seats allocatable per priority level:\n```go\nMaxSeatsTracker interface {\n    TrackMaxSeats(priorityLevelName string, maxSeats uint64)\n}\n```\n\n**Customization**: Implement to enforce policy limits, integrate with external capacity planning\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications and Failure Recovery\n\n### 6.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n**Latency profile**:\n- **Exempt requests**: Microseconds (no queue lookup)\n- **Non-exempt, immediate dispatch**: Milliseconds (lock + shuffle sharding + metrics)\n- **Queued requests**: Seconds to minutes (depends on queue depth, server load)\n\n**Lock contention**:\n- Single lock protects all QueueSet state\n- Lock hold time: O(log queues) for queue selection + O(1) for dispatch\n- Acceptable for typical queue counts; may bottleneck at >100 queues\n\n**Memory overhead per request**: ~1 KB (request wrapper, FIFO node, promise object)\n\n### 6.2 Debugging and Monitoring\n\n**Debug endpoints** (registered by controller):\n- `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_priority_levels`: Current concurrency limits, high-water marks\n- `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_queues`: Queue lengths, virtual time progression, seat counts\n- `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_requests`: Per-request details (user, arrival time, elapsed time)\n\n**Key metrics**:\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_queue_length_after_enqueue`: Snapshot of queue depth after enqueue\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total`: Counter of requests leaving queue\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total`: Counter by reason (queue-full, concurrency-limit)\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_wait_duration_seconds`: Histogram of queue wait time\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_execution_duration_seconds`: Histogram of execution time\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total`: Counter of virtual time wraparound events\n\n**Alerts to monitor**:\n- High rejection rate: indicates server overload or misconfigured limits\n- High queue wait latency: indicates bottleneck at priority level\n- Epoch advance spikes: indicates arithmetic overflow risk (should be rare)\n\n### 6.3 Configuration Mistakes and Recovery\n\n**Misconfiguration examples**:\n\n| Mistake | Symptom | Fix |\n|---------|---------|-----|\n| QueueLengthLimit too low | High rejection rate | Increase limit via PLC update |\n| ConcurrencyLimit too low | High queue depth, timeout | Increase limit, check work estimates |\n| HandSize > numQueues | Shuffle sharding ineffective | Reduce HandSize or increase queues |\n| Work estimate too high | Underutilization of capacity | Lower max seats in work estimator |\n| Conflicting FlowSchemas | Requests matched incorrectly | Review FlowSchema matching rules and order |\n\n**Rollback procedure**:\n- APF is stateless; old config replaces new immediately\n- No in-flight request disruption (queues drain gracefully)\n- No data loss\n\n### 6.4 Scaling and Resource Planning\n\n**Planning for growth**:\n\n1. **Estimate seat demand**: Monitor `apiserver_flowcontrol_seat_demand_*` metrics\n2. **Allocate concurrency**: Adjust `nominalCL` per priority level; total must fit within `--max-requests`\n3. **Right-size queues**: QueueLengthLimit = desired queue depth / numQueues (typically 5–50 requests per queue)\n4. **Monitor latency**: Check `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_wait_duration_seconds` histogram; aim for p99 < 5 seconds\n\n**Capacity planning formula**:\n```\nserverConcurrencyLimit ≤ --max-requests flag\n= sum(priorityLevel.nominalCL) + borrowing headroom\n```\n\n### 6.5 Shutdown and Graceful Draining\n\n**Controller shutdown**:\n1. ConfigQueue stops accepting new config changes\n2. Existing priority levels remain active until Stop() returns\n3. Running requests continue to completion; new requests still enqueued\n\n**Graceful drain**:\n- Set QueueSet to \"quiescing\" when undesired\n- QueueSet removed only when all requests complete\n- Prevents abrupt request cancellation\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directory Map\n\n### Core QueueSet Implementation\n| File | Lines | Purpose |\n|------|-------|---------|\n| `fairqueuing/interface.go` | 27–50 | QueueSet, Request, QueueSetFactory interfaces |\n| `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go` | 85–167 | queueSet struct, StartRequest, dispatch algorithm |\n| `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go` | 31–139 | request, queue, queueSum types |\n| `fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go` | 42–67 | FIFO queue implementation with aggregation |\n\n### Controller and Configuration\n| File | Lines | Purpose |\n|------|-------|---------|\n| `apf_controller.go` | 116–194 | configController, priorityLevelState |\n| `apf_controller.go` | 371–391 | Run loop, borrowing adjustment |\n| `apf_controller.go` | 399–496 | Seat demand tracking, concurrency rebalancing |\n| `apf_filter.go` | 155–198 | Handle method, request classification |\n\n### Supporting Infrastructure\n| File | Lines | Purpose |\n|------|-------|---------|\n| `request/width.go` | 32–90 | WorkEstimate, WorkEstimatorFunc |\n| `fairqueuing/integrator.go` | 29–48 | Integrator interface, seat demand stats |\n| `metrics/metrics.go` | (varies) | Metric definitions and recording |\n| `debug/dump.go` | (varies) | QueueSetDump, debug output |\n\n### Testing\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `queueset/queueset_test.go` | Fairness verification, unit tests |\n| `controller_test.go` | Integration tests with mock configs |\n| `apf_filter_test.go` | End-to-end request flow tests |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Case Studies: Fairness in Practice\n\n### 8.1 Scenario: Mixed Workload (LIST + GET)\n\n**Setup**:\n- Priority level with 8 queues\n- ConcurrencyLimit = 40 seats\n- Flow A: LIST /pods (3 seats per request)\n- Flow B: GET /pod/name (1 seat per request)\n\n**Behavior**:\n1. Both flows enqueue; shuffle sharding assigns each to different queue\n2. Virtual time advances at rate = min(seats_requested, 40) / num_active_queues\n3. Flow A requests dispatch 3 times slower than Flow B (work-aware)\n4. Over time: A gets ~30 seats, B gets ~10 seats (proportional to work)\n5. Result: Predictable latency, neither starves\n\n### 8.2 Scenario: Overload (Rejection)\n\n**Setup**:\n- ConcurrencyLimit = 100\n- QueueLengthLimit = 50\n- Sustained load: 200 requests/sec\n\n**Behavior**:\n1. First 100 requests execute (reach concurrency limit)\n2. Next 400 requests (50/queue × 8 queues) queue\n3. Requests beyond 500 total rejected with 429 Too Many Requests\n4. When load drops, queued requests resume; no cascade rejection\n\n### 8.3 Scenario: Dynamic Borrowing\n\n**Setup**:\n- Priority level 1 (user requests): nominalCL = 50\n- Priority level 2 (system requests): nominalCL = 30\n- Server limit = 80\n\n**Behavior**:\n1. User requests start slow (demand ≈ 20 seats); system requests high (demand ≈ 40 seats)\n2. Every 10 seconds: borrowing recalculates\n   - System gets 50 seats (nominal + borrowed 20 from user level)\n   - User level gets 30 seats (nominal - lent 20)\n3. When user load spikes: recalculation shifts seats back\n4. Result: Server capacity used efficiently; no static waste\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Kubernetes APF QueueSet is a production-grade implementation of virtual-time fairness that achieves:\n\n1. **Fairness guarantee**: Queues with equal work receive equal service over time\n2. **Work awareness**: Wide requests fairly charged proportionally to their resource consumption\n3. **Burst absorption**: Overloads queue gracefully rather than reject immediately\n4. **Operational control**: Dynamic rebalancing via seat demand integrator and borrowing algorithm\n5. **Debuggability**: Rich metrics and dump endpoints for troubleshooting\n\nThe main tradeoff is architectural simplicity: the implementation prioritizes predictable fairness over minimal latency or maximum throughput. The round-robin queue selection and virtual time synchronization on every lock acquisition add overhead, but this is acceptable for typical Kubernetes cluster sizes where fairness is more critical than microsecond-level latency.\n\n---\n\n## References to Implementation\n\n**Key entry points for further exploration**:\n1. Review `syncTimeLocked()` and `advanceEpoch()` to understand virtual time mechanics\n4. Study `updateBorrowingLocked()` to see dynamic concurrency allocation\n5. It addresses a fundamental tension in server fairness: how to allocate limited resources fairly among competing clients while maintaining low latency and predictable behavior. This document explains the subsystem's architecture, control flow, fairness algorithm, and operational tradeoffs.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### Purpose\nThe QueueSet subsystem ensures that API server resources are distributed fairly and predictably across different request flows (identified by FlowSchemas and distinguished by client identity or other flow characteristics). Unlike simple first-come-first-served or priority queuing, APF QueueSet provides:\n\n- **Fairness among flows**: Each flow gets a proportional share of server capacity\n- **Burst absorption**: Temporary overloads are queued rather than rejected immediately\n- **Virtual-time fairness**: Queues that have received less service get higher dispatch priority\n- **Work-aware scheduling**: Request \"width\" (concurrency cost) is accounted for, not just count\n\n### Architectural Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n- **APF Filter** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go`): Entry point that classifies requests into FlowSchemas and invokes QueueSet\n- **APF Controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`): Manages FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration CRDs, reconfigures QueueSets dynamically\n- **Work Estimator** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go`): Estimates how many \"seats\" (concurrent slots) a request occupies based on operation type, object count, or watch size\n\n**Downstream users:**\n- HTTP request processing pipeline: Requests flow through StartRequest → queue or immediate dispatch → Finish\n- Metrics collection: QueueSet emits concurrency, latency, and fairness metrics\n\n**No external dependencies:**\n- QueueSet is completely self-contained; it does not interact with other Kubernetes subsystems beyond the filter/controller/estimator layer\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Abstraction Layer (`fairqueuing/interface.go`)\n\n**QueueSetFactory**\n- Creates QueueSets during controller startup and reconfiguration\n- Two-phase construction: `BeginConstruction` (validates config, allocates metrics) → `Complete` (finalizes with concurrency limit)\n- Rationale: Early validation prevents resource exhaustion from bad configs\n\n**QueueSet Interface**\n- Minimal public API: `StartRequest()`, `IsIdle()`, `Dump()`\n- `StartRequest` either: (1) immediately dispatches exempt requests, (2) queues non-exempt requests, or (3) rejects due to concurrency/queue limits\n- Returns a `Request` object that the caller must `Finish()` exactly once\n\n### 2.2 QueueSet Implementation (`queueset/queueset.go`)\n\n**Main QueueSet struct** (lines 85–167)\n- Fields before lock: immutable configuration (clock, metrics gauges, estimated service duration)\n- Fields after lock: mutable state (queues, virtual time R, executing request count, seat tracking)\n\n**Key state fields:**\n- `queues`: Array of `queue` objects, length determined by `DesiredNumQueues` (shuffle-sharding parameter)\n- `currentR`: Global virtual time, expressed in seat-seconds. Monotonically increases, wraps to prevent overflow\n- `totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`: Track resource usage; used for concurrency limit enforcement\n- `totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`: Request counts per phase\n- `robinIndex`: Round-robin pointer for fair queue selection during dispatch\n\n### 2.3 Request Container (`queueset/types.go`)\n\n**request struct** (lines 31–82)\n- Temporary wrapper around a logical request\n- Tracks: context, queue assignment, work estimate, decision promise, arrival time, timestamps\n- Two decision states: `decisionExecute` (dispatch from queue) or `decisionCancel` (timeout)\n- `arrivalR`: Virtual time at enqueue; used to compute virtual finish time\n\n**queue struct** (lines 93–110)\n- `requestsWaiting`: FIFO list of queued requests\n- `requestsExecuting`: Set of actively executing requests from this queue\n- `nextDispatchR`: Virtual finish time of the next request to be dispatched from this queue\n- `seatsInUse`: Current seat count occupied by executing requests\n\n### 2.4 FIFO List with Aggregation (`queueset/fifo_list.go`)\n\n**requestFIFO**\n- Wrapper around Go's `container/list`\n- Maintains running sum (`queueSum`) of initial seats, max seats, and total work across all waiting requests\n- This aggregation enables O(1) queue selection heuristic during shuffle sharding\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Request Initialization Phase\n\n**Entry point: APF Filter (`apf_filter.go:155–198`)**\n```\nHandle(ctx, requestDigest, noteFn, workEstimator, queueNoteFn, execFn)\n```\n\n1. **Classification**: Delegate to controller's `startRequest()` to classify request into FlowSchema/PriorityLevel\n2. **Work estimation**: Call `workEstimator()` to get `WorkEstimate` (InitialSeats, FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency)\n3. **Decision**: Receive `Request` object or nil (rejection)\n4. **Execution**: Call `Request.Finish(execFn)` which:\n   - Waits on virtual queue decision promise\n   - Executes user's HTTP handler\n   - Calls `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()`\n\n### 3.2 Controller Configuration and Startup (`apf_controller.go:371–391`)\n\n**Run() method:**\n1. Waits for FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration informers to sync\n2. Starts config worker goroutine: reads API objects, populates `priorityLevelStates` map\n3. Starts borrowing adjustment goroutine: every 10 seconds, rebalances concurrency limits between priority levels based on seat demand statistics\n\n**lockAndDigestConfigObjects()**: Atomically rebuilds priority level state from FlowSchema specs\n- Ensures backward compatibility: old queue drains before removal\n\n### 3.3 QueueSet.StartRequest() Flow (`queueset.go:308–356`)\n\n**Step 0: Handle exempt priority levels (DesiredNumQueues < 1)**\n- If `DesiredNumQueues ≤ 0`, check only concurrency limit (no queuing)\n- If seats can be accommodated, call `dispatchSansQueueLocked()`: immediately start execution, return request with decision pre-set to `decisionExecute`\n- Otherwise reject and return nil\n\n**Step 1: Shuffle sharding and enqueue (`shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked` lines 552–579)**\n\na. **Shuffle sharding** (`shuffleShardLocked` lines 583–612):\n   - Hash the flow distinguisher (user, namespace, etc.) into a \"hand\" of HandSize queues\n   - Among the hand, pick the queue with minimum total waiting work (seat-seconds)\n   - Rationale: Distributes flows evenly; overloaded flows don't monopolize single queue\n   - Implementation: Uses `shufflesharding.Dealer` (cryptographic shuffle permutation)\n\nb. **Enqueue** (`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked` lines 618–629):\n   - Check: `totSeatsInUse ≥ ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength ≥ QueueLengthLimit`\n   - If true, reject (return nil)\n   - Otherwise, enqueue to FIFO, set request decision promise to `decisionCancel` (default), return request object\n\nc. **Queue initialization**:\n   - If queue was idle, set `nextDispatchR = currentR` (queue inherits global virtual time)\n\n**Step 2: Dispatch loop (`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` lines 654–657)**\n```go\nfor totRequestsWaiting > 0 && totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit && dispatchLocked() {\n}\n```\n- Repeatedly calls `dispatchLocked()` while:\n  - Requests are waiting\n  - Room under concurrency limit\n- Stops when any condition fails or no more requests can be dispatched\n\n### 3.4 Dispatch Algorithm: Virtual Time Fairness (`dispatchLocked` lines 695–743)\n\n**Finding next queue to serve (`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` lines 776–844):**\n\n1. **Round-robin scan** of all queues, searching for highest-priority queue\n2. **Priority metric**: Virtual finish time of oldest request: `minVirtualFinish = nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()`\n3. **Select queue** with minimum virtual finish time\n4. **Round-robin tiebreaker**: If tied, advance robin pointer to favor lower-index queue next iteration\n\n**Dispatching request from chosen queue:**\n\n1. **Seat check**: `canAccommodateSeatsLocked()` verifies max seat requirement fits\n   - Special case: if request width > ConcurrencyLimit and other requests executing, reject\n   - Rationale: Prevent scenarios where single wide request blocks everything\n\n2. **Dequeue and update state**:\n   - Remove from waiting FIFO\n   - Set decision promise to `decisionExecute` (wakes waiting Finish goroutine)\n   - Add to queue's `requestsExecuting` set\n   - Increment `totRequestsExecuting`, `totSeatsInUse`\n\n3. **Update virtual time**:\n   - `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()`\n   - This advances the queue's virtual time, preventing it from repeatedly winning\n\n4. **Anti-windup**: Call `boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)` to prevent virtual time overflow (see section 3.5)\n\n### 3.5 Virtual Time Synchronization and Overflow Prevention (`syncTimeLocked` lines 465–479, `advanceEpoch` lines 492–522)\n\n**syncTimeLocked()** is called whenever lock is acquired:\n```\ncurrentR += virtualTimeRatio * (now - lastRealTime)\n```\n\n- `virtualTimeRatio = min(seatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / numActiveQueues`\n- Rationale: Virtual time advances proportional to server load; more loaded servers have faster virtual clocks\n- Effect: Queues sharing equally will dispatch equally (fairness guarantee)\n\n**Epoch advancement** (line 475):\n- When `currentR ≥ highR` (rDecrement + rDecrement/2), subtract `rDecrement` from:\n  - Global `currentR`\n  - All `queue.nextDispatchR` values\n  - All `request.arrivalR` values\n- Prevents overflow of 64-bit `SeatSeconds` accumulator\n- Records metric: `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total`\n\n### 3.6 Request Completion (`finishRequestLocked` lines 863–902, `wait` method lines 397–441)\n\n**Request.Finish(execFn) sequence:**\n\n1. **Wait for decision** (`wait()` lines 397–441):\n   - Call `req.decision.Get()` (blocking read from promise)\n   - Acquire lock and sync virtual time\n   - If decision is `decisionExecute`, return true\n   - If decision is `decisionCancel` (timeout), remove from queue, return false\n\n2. **Execute handler** (callback):\n   - Run user's HTTP handler with defer for cleanup\n\n3. **Release seats and dispatch more** (`finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible` lines 851–858):\n   - Decrement seat counts\n   - Remove from queue\n   - Call `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` to drain any waiting requests\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Concurrency Limits\n\n**Server-level limit**: Set by operator via `--max-requests` flag\n- Hard cap on total executing requests across all priority levels\n- Prevents server from being overwhelmed\n\n**Priority-level limit**: Configured per PriorityLevelConfiguration\n- `nominalCL`: configured concurrency limit\n- `currentCL`: dynamically adjusted every 10 seconds based on seat demand\n- Borrowing: priority levels can borrow from each other if demand is uneven (see section 4.4)\n\n**Queue-level limit**: `QueueLengthLimit` requests per queue\n- If `totSeatsInUse ≥ ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength ≥ QueueLengthLimit`, reject new request\n- Rationale: Prevents unbounded memory growth; tail latencies become unacceptable\n\n**Seat accounting**: Each request occupies \"seats\" during execution\n- `InitialSeats`: while request is being processed\n- `FinalSeats`: during `AdditionalLatency` (cleanup/response streaming)\n- Rationale: Wide requests (LIST) fairly charged more; prevents resource exhaustion\n\n### 4.2 Request Rejection\n\nRequests are rejected (filter returns 429 Too Many Requests) when:\n\n1. **Concurrency limit reached** AND queue is full: `totSeatsInUse ≥ ConcurrencyLimit AND queueLength ≥ QueueLengthLimit`\n2. **Queue full only** (in some cases): if queue already has QueueLengthLimit requests\n3. **Work exceeds server capacity**: if single request width > ConcurrencyLimit and other requests executing\n\n**Metrics**: `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` labeled by priority level and rejection reason\n\n### 4.3 Request Timeouts\n\n**Queue wait timeout**: Controlled by client context deadline\n- If request context is cancelled or times out while queued, decision is set to `decisionCancel` in `wait()`\n- Request is removed from queue, metrics updated, request fails\n\n**No server-side timeout**: APF does not impose timeouts; relies on client (or gateway) timeout\n\n**Metrics**: `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_queue_depth_after_enqueue` and latency histograms\n\n### 4.4 Seat Demand and Dynamic Borrowing\n\n**Seat demand tracking** (`priorityLevelState.seatDemandIntegrator`):\n- Integrator tracks seat demand (executing + waiting seats) over time\n- Every 10 seconds, `updateBorrowingLocked()` samples and smooths seat demand\n\n**Concurrency limit adjustment**:\n- Non-exempt priority levels: `currentCL = max(minCL, min(nominalCL, smoothedDemand))`\n- Exempt priority levels: uncapped, but `currentCL = max(minCL, highWatermarkDemand)`\n- Rebalancing algorithm: allocates remaining server concurrency among priority levels proportional to smoothed demand\n- If server capacity exhausted, priority levels can share fairly via this algorithm\n\n**Tradeoff**: Borrowing adds latency (10-second reaction time) but prevents static over-allocation\n\n### 4.5 Virtual Time Fairness Guarantees and Limitations\n\n**Fairness property**: If queue i has `ni` waiting requests and queue j has `nj` waiting requests, and both occupy same number of seats, they will be dispatched in proportion `ni : nj` over time (amortized).\n\n**Limitation 1: Work variance**:\n- If requests have widely varying work estimates, variance in service time is unavoidable\n- Example: LIST (wide) and GET (narrow) requests queued together will have different latencies\n\n**Limitation 2: Priority levels (not within-priority fairness)**:\n- QueueSet only guarantees fairness among queues *within* a priority level\n- Inter-priority fairness is handled by concurrency limit allocation (borrowing mechanism)\n- Exempt priority levels bypass QueueSet entirely (no fairness guarantee)\n\n**Limitation 3: Round-robin bias**:\n- `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()` uses round-robin with virtual finish time tiebreaking\n- This introduces slight bias toward lower-index queues; acceptable in practice\n\n### 4.6 Architectural Tradeoffs\n\n| Tradeoff | Choice | Rationale |\n|----------|--------|-----------|\n| **Queuing vs rejection** | Queue first, reject on overflow | Better isolation; allows recovery when load drops |\n| **Shuffle sharding** | Distribute flows across HandSize queues | Prevents single bad actor from blocking entire priority level |\n| **Virtual time scale** | Seat-seconds, not requests | Work-aware fairness; wide requests fairly charged |\n| **Dynamic borrowing** | 10-second rebalancing interval | Coarse grained to avoid thrashing; fast enough for most workloads |\n| **Two-phase config** | BeginConstruction → Complete | Allows rollback if downstream config invalid |\n| **Round-robin dispatch** | Linear scan of all queues | O(n) per dispatch, acceptable for typical queue counts (~8) |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 QueueSetFactory Pluggability\n\n**Location**: `fairqueuing/interface.go:27–42`\n\nOperators can substitute custom `QueueSetFactory` implementations by passing to `TestableConfig`:\n```go\nconfig.QueueSetFactory = customFactory\n```\n\n**Customization examples**:\n- Different shuffle sharding strategies (e.g., deterministic vs random)\n- Alternative FIFO implementations (e.g., priority heap instead of FIFO)\n- Custom virtual time advancement formulas\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect implementation breaks fairness guarantees; requires deep understanding of algorithm\n\n### 5.2 Work Estimator Customization\n\n**Location**: `request/width.go:75–136`\n\n`NewWorkEstimator()` takes pluggable functions:\n- `statsGetterFunc`: Get object count for LIST requests\n- `watchCountGetterFunc`: Get watch listener count for WATCH requests\n- `maxSeatsFunc`: Override maximum seats per priority level\n\n**Current implementation**:\n- LIST/WATCH: seats proportional to object count\n- CREATE/UPDATE/PATCH/DELETE: seats based on watch listeners affected\n- Other verbs: 1 seat\n\n**Risk**: Seat overestimation wastes capacity; underestimation allows resource exhaustion\n\n### 5.3 Clock Abstraction\n\n**Location**: `fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go` (not shown, but imported)\n\nQueueSet uses interface clock, not `time.Now()` directly:\n```go\nclock eventclock.Interface\n```\n\n**Customization**: Inject mock clock for deterministic testing\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect clock causes virtual time disorders; must be monotonic\n\n### 5.4 Priority Level Configuration CRD\n\n**Location**: Kubernetes API, read by controller\n\nOperators can define custom `PriorityLevelConfiguration` and `FlowSchema` objects:\n- Adjust concurrency limits\n- Define flow distinguishers (user, namespace, etc.)\n- Create custom priority levels\n\n**Risk**: Config errors cascade to all requests; controller must validate before applying\n\n### 5.5 MaxSeatsTracker Hook\n\n**Location**: `apf_controller.go:156–160`, `apf_filter.go:81–83`\n\nController tracks maximum seats allocatable per priority level:\n```go\nMaxSeatsTracker interface {\n    TrackMaxSeats(priorityLevelName string, maxSeats uint64)\n}\n```\n\n**Customization**: Implement to enforce policy limits, integrate with external capacity planning\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications and Failure Recovery\n\n### 6.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n**Latency profile**:\n- **Exempt requests**: Microseconds (no queue lookup)\n- **Non-exempt, immediate dispatch**: Milliseconds (lock + shuffle sharding + metrics)\n- **Queued requests**: Seconds to minutes (depends on queue depth, server load)\n\n**Lock contention**:\n- Single lock protects all QueueSet state\n- Lock hold time: O(log queues) for queue selection + O(1) for dispatch\n- Acceptable for typical queue counts; may bottleneck at >100 queues\n\n**Memory overhead per request**: ~1 KB (request wrapper, FIFO node, promise object)\n\n### 6.2 Debugging and Monitoring\n\n**Debug endpoints** (registered by controller):\n- `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_priority_levels`: Current concurrency limits, high-water marks\n- `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_queues`: Queue lengths, virtual time progression, seat counts\n- `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_requests`: Per-request details (user, arrival time, elapsed time)\n\n**Key metrics**:\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_queue_length_after_enqueue`: Snapshot of queue depth after enqueue\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total`: Counter of requests leaving queue\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total`: Counter by reason (queue-full, concurrency-limit)\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_wait_duration_seconds`: Histogram of queue wait time\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_execution_duration_seconds`: Histogram of execution time\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total`: Counter of virtual time wraparound events\n\n**Alerts to monitor**:\n- High rejection rate: indicates server overload or misconfigured limits\n- High queue wait latency: indicates bottleneck at priority level\n- Epoch advance spikes: indicates arithmetic overflow risk (should be rare)\n\n### 6.3 Configuration Mistakes and Recovery\n\n**Misconfiguration examples**:\n\n| Mistake | Symptom | Fix |\n|---------|---------|-----|\n| QueueLengthLimit too low | High rejection rate | Increase limit via PLC update |\n| ConcurrencyLimit too low | High queue depth, timeout | Increase limit, check work estimates |\n| HandSize > numQueues | Shuffle sharding ineffective | Reduce HandSize or increase queues |\n| Work estimate too high | Underutilization of capacity | Lower max seats in work estimator |\n| Conflicting FlowSchemas | Requests matched incorrectly | Review FlowSchema matching rules and order |\n\n**Rollback procedure**:\n- APF is stateless; old config replaces new immediately\n- No in-flight request disruption (queues drain gracefully)\n- No data loss\n\n### 6.4 Scaling and Resource Planning\n\n**Planning for growth**:\n\n1. **Estimate seat demand**: Monitor `apiserver_flowcontrol_seat_demand_*` metrics\n2. **Allocate concurrency**: Adjust `nominalCL` per priority level; total must fit within `--max-requests`\n3. **Right-size queues**: QueueLengthLimit = desired queue depth / numQueues (typically 5–50 requests per queue)\n4. **Monitor latency**: Check `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_wait_duration_seconds` histogram; aim for p99 < 5 seconds\n\n**Capacity planning formula**:\n```\nserverConcurrencyLimit ≤ --max-requests flag\n= sum(priorityLevel.nominalCL) + borrowing headroom\n```\n\n### 6.5 Shutdown and Graceful Draining\n\n**Controller shutdown**:\n1. ConfigQueue stops accepting new config changes\n2. Existing priority levels remain active until Stop() returns\n3. Running requests continue to completion; new requests still enqueued\n\n**Graceful drain**:\n- Set QueueSet to \"quiescing\" when undesired\n- QueueSet removed only when all requests complete\n- Prevents abrupt request cancellation\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directory Map\n\n### Core QueueSet Implementation\n| File | Lines | Purpose |\n|------|-------|---------|\n| `fairqueuing/interface.go` | 27–50 | QueueSet, Request, QueueSetFactory interfaces |\n| `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go` | 85–167 | queueSet struct, StartRequest, dispatch algorithm |\n| `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go` | 31–139 | request, queue, queueSum types |\n| `fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go` | 42–67 | FIFO queue implementation with aggregation |\n\n### Controller and Configuration\n| File | Lines | Purpose |\n|------|-------|---------|\n| `apf_controller.go` | 116–194 | configController, priorityLevelState |\n| `apf_controller.go` | 371–391 | Run loop, borrowing adjustment |\n| `apf_controller.go` | 399–496 | Seat demand tracking, concurrency rebalancing |\n| `apf_filter.go` | 155–198 | Handle method, request classification |\n\n### Supporting Infrastructure\n| File | Lines | Purpose |\n|------|-------|---------|\n| `request/width.go` | 32–90 | WorkEstimate, WorkEstimatorFunc |\n| `fairqueuing/integrator.go` | 29–48 | Integrator interface, seat demand stats |\n| `metrics/metrics.go` | (varies) | Metric definitions and recording |\n| `debug/dump.go` | (varies) | QueueSetDump, debug output |\n\n### Testing\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `queueset/queueset_test.go` | Fairness verification, unit tests |\n| `controller_test.go` | Integration tests with mock configs |\n| `apf_filter_test.go` | End-to-end request flow tests |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Case Studies: Fairness in Practice\n\n### 8.1 Scenario: Mixed Workload (LIST + GET)\n\n**Setup**:\n- Priority level with 8 queues\n- ConcurrencyLimit = 40 seats\n- Flow A: LIST /pods (3 seats per request)\n- Flow B: GET /pod/name (1 seat per request)\n\n**Behavior**:\n1. Both flows enqueue; shuffle sharding assigns each to different queue\n2. Virtual time advances at rate = min(seats_requested, 40) / num_active_queues\n3. Flow A requests dispatch 3 times slower than Flow B (work-aware)\n4. Over time: A gets ~30 seats, B gets ~10 seats (proportional to work)\n5. Result: Predictable latency, neither starves\n\n### 8.2 Scenario: Overload (Rejection)\n\n**Setup**:\n- ConcurrencyLimit = 100\n- QueueLengthLimit = 50\n- Sustained load: 200 requests/sec\n\n**Behavior**:\n1. First 100 requests execute (reach concurrency limit)\n2. Next 400 requests (50/queue × 8 queues) queue\n3. Requests beyond 500 total rejected with 429 Too Many Requests\n4. When load drops, queued requests resume; no cascade rejection\n\n### 8.3 Scenario: Dynamic Borrowing\n\n**Setup**:\n- Priority level 1 (user requests): nominalCL = 50\n- Priority level 2 (system requests): nominalCL = 30\n- Server limit = 80\n\n**Behavior**:\n1. User requests start slow (demand ≈ 20 seats); system requests high (demand ≈ 40 seats)\n2. Every 10 seconds: borrowing recalculates\n   - System gets 50 seats (nominal + borrowed 20 from user level)\n   - User level gets 30 seats (nominal - lent 20)\n3. When user load spikes: recalculation shifts seats back\n4. Result: Server capacity used efficiently; no static waste\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Kubernetes APF QueueSet is a production-grade implementation of virtual-time fairness that achieves:\n\n1. **Fairness guarantee**: Queues with equal work receive equal service over time\n2. **Work awareness**: Wide requests fairly charged proportionally to their resource consumption\n3. **Burst absorption**: Overloads queue gracefully rather than reject immediately\n4. **Operational control**: Dynamic rebalancing via seat demand integrator and borrowing algorithm\n5. **Debuggability**: Rich metrics and dump endpoints for troubleshooting\n\nThe main tradeoff is architectural simplicity: the implementation prioritizes predictable fairness over minimal latency or maximum throughput. The round-robin queue selection and virtual time synchronization on every lock acquisition add overhead, but this is acceptable for typical Kubernetes cluster sizes where fairness is more critical than microsecond-level latency.\n\n---\n\n## References to Implementation\n\n**Key entry points for further exploration**:\n1. Start with `QueueSet.StartRequest()` to understand request intake\n2. Follow `dispatchLocked()` to see virtual time fairness in action\n3. Review `syncTimeLocked()` and `advanceEpoch()` to understand virtual time mechanics\n4. Study `updateBorrowingLocked()` to see dynamic concurrency allocation\n5. Trace metrics recording in `queueset.go` to understand observability\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
